## Original Specification
<prompt_content>
<pdd-dependency>agentic_common_python.prompt</pdd-dependency>
<pdd-dependency>checkup_review_loop_python.prompt</pdd-dependency>
<pdd-dependency>checkup_gates_python.prompt</pdd-dependency>

1) This module acts as the multi-step agentic orchestrator for the `pdd checkup` command, responsible for managing an 8-step workflow that analyzes, fixes, and verifies software issues. It coordinates between LLM-based agents, local environment execution, and git state management, ensuring that changes are isolated in worktrees and that the workflow can be resumed gracefully after interruptions.

2) Requirements:
    1. Implement an 8-step workflow: 1. Discover, 2. Deps, 3. Build, 4. Interfaces, 5. Test, 6. Fix (split into 6.1 Fix, 6.2 Regression, 6.3 E2E), 7. Verify, and 8. Create PR.
    2. Manage an iterative "Fix-Verify" loop for steps 3-7; if Step 7 does not contain the string "All Issues Fixed", the workflow should loop back to Step 3, up to a maximum of `MAX_FIX_VERIFY_ITERATIONS` (default 3). If the maximum is reached without that exact signal, return failure and do not push fixes or create/skip through a successful PR gate.
    3. Ensure process isolation by creating and operating within a git worktree for all fix-related steps (Steps 6-8). The worktree must include both uncommitted changes and untracked files from the main repository.
    4. Provide robust resume support by persisting the workflow state (last completed step, outputs, costs, worktree path, AND `mode` ∈ {"issue", "pr"}, AND `pr_number`, `pr_owner`, `pr_repo`, `pr_head_sha` when in PR mode) to a local `.pdd/checkup-state` directory and optionally to GitHub comments. When loading state, validate four identity axes before reuse: (a) `mode` matches the current invocation, (b) `pr_number` matches when both runs are PR-mode, (c) `pr_owner/pr_repo` matches when both are present, (d) `pr_head_sha` is non-empty on both the cached state and current PR metadata and the values are equal. ANY mismatch or missing PR head SHA discards the cached state and forces a fresh setup — the same `issue_number` can verify different PRs over time, and reusing a stale `.pdd/worktrees/checkup-pr-A` path during a verification of PR B silently runs all subsequent steps against the wrong code. When the saved worktree path is missing on resume, recreate it via the SAME helper that originally built it: `_setup_pr_worktree(...)` for PR mode (using saved `pr_owner/pr_repo/pr_number`), `_setup_worktree(...)` for issue mode. Calling the issue-mode helper on a PR-mode resume would silently rebuild from HEAD instead of the PR head.
    5. Handle fractional steps (e.g., 6.1, 6.2) for internal logic and template loading, while mapping them to user-friendly labels (e.g., 6a, 6b) in the console output.
    6. Support a `--no-fix` mode which runs analysis steps (1-5) and verification (7) linearly without creating worktrees or PRs.
    7. Support a PR-verification mode (orchestrator parameters `pr_url`, `pr_owner`, `pr_repo`, `pr_number`). When `pr_mode` is true:
       - Set up the worktree via `_setup_pr_worktree(cwd, pr_owner, pr_repo, pr_number, quiet)` BEFORE Step 1 so all subsequent steps see the PR's code, not HEAD.
       - IMMEDIATELY after `_setup_pr_worktree` (and again on resume after restoring the worktree path), call `_refresh_pr_context_from_worktree(context, worktree_path)` to overwrite `context["project_root"]`, `context["architecture_json"]`, and `context["pddrc_content"]` with values loaded from the PR worktree. `run_agentic_checkup` loaded these from the pre-worktree `cwd` and passed them into the orchestrator; without the refresh, prompts audit stale architecture/config and miss PR-introduced changes to architecture.json or `.pddrc` (round-5 Finding 3). The parent `cwd` itself stays unchanged — gh CLI auth and workflow-state persistence run against the original checkout.
       - After the PR worktree is available, refresh the PR base branch into a dedicated local tracking ref, then derive a concise merge-base changed-file summary and store it in `context["pr_changed_files"]` so Step 5 and Step 7 can run PR-scoped tests before attempting any full-suite command. Use local git (`git diff --name-status --find-renames <refreshed-pr-base>...HEAD`) against that refreshed ref. Never use stale `origin/<base>` when PR metadata is available, and never fall back to `HEAD~1`; on multi-commit PRs that silently collapses scope to the last commit. If the PR base cannot be refreshed locally, store an explanatory unavailable string so prompts stay well-formed while agents test conservatively.
       - Resolve the PR's source repo via `pr_owner/pr_repo` (NOT a hardcoded `origin`): walk `git remote -v` looking for a remote whose URL matches `pr_owner/pr_repo`; if none, fetch via the explicit URL `https://github.com/{pr_owner}/{pr_repo}.git pull/{pr_number}/head:{branch_name}`. This is what makes fork-PR verification actually work — a clone of `myfork/repo` cannot fetch `pull/N/head` from `origin` when the PR lives on `upstream/repo`.
       - In full fix mode (`no_fix=False`), run Steps 1-7 against the PR worktree. After the fix/verify loop, commit eligible generated changes with the bot identity and push them back to the PR head branch using PR metadata (`head.repo.clone_url`, `head.ref`, `head.repo.owner.login`, `head.repo.name`). Missing metadata or push failure is a hard failure because fixes must not remain silently local.
       - Step 7 must not post GitHub comments in PR mode. The orchestrator owns posting the canonical PR/issue final report and MUST post it on every PR-mode terminal path (gate pass after push, gate fail, max-iteration exhaustion, registry/prompt-source guard refusals, push failure, post-push reverify abort, `--no-fix` gate pass/fail). `_post_pr_mode_final_report` returns a `status_suffix` string — empty when both posts succeeded, otherwise containing a pointer to `.pdd/checkup-pr-<n>/final-report.md`. Callers MUST append the suffix to whatever message they return so pdd-issue/pdd_cloud surfaces show the partial-post condition. The helper persists `step_outputs["pr_post_status"]` for state inspection. Comment-post failures MUST NOT flip the gate outcome — gh / network flakiness is independent of code-verification truth (round-5 Finding 4).
       - Skip Step 8 entirely (the PR already exists; the job is to verify and improve it, not open another).
       - **PR-head freshness lease (issue #1116)**: in PR fix mode (not `--no-fix`), bound auto-rerun when the remote PR head advances mid-checkup. Cap restarts at `MAX_PR_HEAD_REFRESHES = 2`. Four freshness checkpoints raise an internal `_PRHeadAdvancedRestart` exception caught by the outer wrapper:
         - **Checkpoint A**: after Step 7's gate passes (`_step7_passed` returns True) but BEFORE the guards-and-push block. Re-fetch PR metadata; if `head_sha` differs from the entry SHA captured at PR-mode start, raise restart.
         - **Checkpoint A2**: after the guards-and-push block's `_fetch_pr_metadata` call but BEFORE the registry/prompt-source guard checks. The two guards each post the canonical Step 7 verdict on refusal; if the head moved between Checkpoint A and now, that verdict belongs to the OLD head. Reuse the just-fetched `pr_metadata["head_sha"]` (no extra GitHub call) and raise restart on mismatch.
         - **Checkpoint B**: when `_commit_and_push_if_changed` returns `(False, push_message)` AND the message indicates a remote-advance-related failure ("Failed to rebase fixes onto updated PR branch", "Failed to refresh PR branch before retrying push", "Failed to reset to original fixer commit before rebase", or generic "Failed to push fixes to PR branch: …" whose embedded git stderr matches `_is_remote_advanced_push_error`). Re-fetch metadata; raise restart only when the fresh `head_sha` actually differs from the entry SHA (auth/network errors must not consume budget).
         - **Checkpoint D**: after EVERY successful `_commit_and_push_if_changed` return — normal push, post-rebase reverify-passed, AND no-change variants ("No changes to push.", "No eligible changes to push."). The check must happen unconditionally on the success path because the round-1 narrow filter on no-change messages left plain-success and rebase-success paths open to a stale verdict when a third party landed commits AFTER our push but BEFORE `_post_pr_mode_final_report`. Baseline is `_git_rev_parse_head(worktree_path)` (the local pushed SHA) — NOT `current_pr_head_sha`. After a real push the remote head moves BECAUSE of us; comparing fresh against entry would false-positive every push. Local HEAD equals our pushed commit on normal/rebase paths and equals entry SHA on the no-change path, so a single Checkpoint D subsumes the round-1 Checkpoint C. Raise restart on mismatch.
       - All checkpoints fail-degrade to current behavior when their baseline SHA is empty or the fresh refetch yields empty — the lease never short-circuits on transient `_fetch_pr_metadata` / `_git_rev_parse_head` failures.
       - **Fix-mode entry-SHA fail-closed**: when fix mode (`no_fix=False`) enters PR mode and the entry `_fetch_pr_metadata` returns an empty `head_sha`, the orchestrator MUST fail-closed immediately — no Step 7, no worktree fix loop, no push. Every fix-mode checkpoint gates on a non-empty `current_pr_head_sha`; without that baseline the entire lease silently disables, opening the same stale-verdict hole the lease was built to close. Symmetric with the `--no-fix` post-Step-7 fail-closed below. Return shape: `(False, "Could not determine entry PR head SHA for PR #N; fix-mode freshness lease requires a baseline. Rerun pdd checkup --pr.", total_cost, last_model_used)`.
       - The public `run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator` is a thin wrapper around an internal `_run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator_inner` that contains the existing 8-step body. Non-PR mode is pass-through. PR mode loops around the inner, catches `_PRHeadAdvancedRestart`, and:
         - Accumulates `cost_so_far` from each iteration into a cumulative return cost.
         - Calls `clear_workflow_state(...)` (best-effort try/except) so a flaky next `_fetch_pr_metadata` returning the OLD SHA cannot defeat the rerun via the resume-state identity guard. The restart exception already proves the head advanced; don't depend on a fresh fetch to re-prove it.
         - Increments and persists a refresh counter at `.pdd/checkup-pr-{pr_number}/pr_head_refreshes` (single int, best-effort I/O) so a Ctrl-C + manual rerun cannot bypass the bound. The sidecar lives OUTSIDE the workflow-state dir so `clear_workflow_state` never deletes it.
         - When `refresh_count >= MAX_PR_HEAD_REFRESHES`, returns failure with a diagnostic that lists every observed `old_sha->new_sha` transition and cites `max_pr_head_refreshes=2`.
         - On clean inner return (success OR failure), removes the sidecar so the next checkup on this PR starts with a full budget.
       - `--no-fix` mode does NOT consume restart budget. The fix-mode checkpoints all guard with `not no_fix`. However, `--no-fix --pr` mode DOES perform its own one-shot head-freshness check: after Step 7's gate passes, refetch the PR head SHA. Fail-closed on THREE conditions (no budget consumed): (a) the fresh SHA differs from the entry SHA (advance confirmed), (b) the refetch fails / returns an empty SHA (freshness unknown after the run), or (c) the entry SHA was empty / unknown when we entered PR mode (freshness unknown before the run). Any one of the three returns `success=False` with a diagnostic, and posts a report body that includes the downgrade reason prepended to the Step 7 output via a `**Verdict downgraded — unverified:**` banner (so the PR/issue thread shows WHY the verdict was invalidated). `_finalize`'s SHA-mismatch downgrade only runs under `--review-loop`, NOT plain `--no-fix --pr`, so the orchestrator owns this guardrail.
       - The lease NEVER force-pushes. `_commit_and_push_if_changed`'s return shape stays `(bool, str)`. `_run_final_checkup_on_pr` in `agentic_e2e_fix_orchestrator.py` remains the outer safety net and is NOT modified by this fix.
       - `_PRHeadAdvancedRestart` carries a `step_comments: Set[int]` field. Every raise site passes the current `step_comments_set`. The outer wrapper preserves this across restart iterations in `preserved_step_comments: Set[int]` and passes it back into the next inner call via `_carried_step_comments: Optional[Set[int]] = None`. When the inner starts with `state is None`, it initialises `step_comments_set` from `_carried_step_comments` (if provided) instead of an empty set, so per-step issue comments are not re-posted after `clear_workflow_state` wipes the persisted field.
       - `_run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator_inner` accepts two additional private kwargs set only by the outer wrapper on restart iterations: `_force_skip_state_load: bool = False` (when True, sets `state = None, loaded_gh_id = None` without calling `load_workflow_state`, defeating any silent GitHub DELETE failure that leaves stale state loadable) and `_carried_step_comments: Optional[Set[int]] = None` (described above). The outer sets `_force_skip_state_load = (refresh_count > 0)` and `_carried_step_comments = preserved_step_comments if refresh_count > 0 else None`.
    8. Implement per-step timeouts and error handling, including a mechanism to abort if agent providers fail consecutively. Classify user-facing aborts as agent execution timeouts only for runner/process timeout wording such as `Timeout expired`, `TimeoutExpired`, `Agent timed out`, or `Step <n> timed out`; generic provider/request/network timeout wording must remain provider failure wording.
    9. **Trusted Step-Comment Flow**: The orchestrator owns visible per-step `## Step N/8:` comments on the GitHub issue, posted via `gh issue comment` with trusted PDD credentials. Step prompts MUST NOT call `gh issue comment` themselves for successful step progress — they emit a single `<step_report>...</step_report>` block in their final response and the orchestrator extracts and posts it once.
        - Import from `pdd.agentic_common`: `extract_step_report(step_output) -> Optional[str]`, `post_step_comment_once(*, repo_owner, repo_name, issue_number, step_num: int, body: str, posted_steps: Set[int], cwd) -> bool`, and `normalize_step_comments_state(raw) -> Set[int]`.
        - **State shape**: `state["step_comments"]` persists as a sorted `List[int]` on disk; hydrate to `Set[int]` via `normalize_step_comments_state` on resume; persist back as a sorted list via `_build_state(..., step_comments=sorted(step_comments_set))` on every save (success, hard-stop, abort).
        - **Composite-key encoding (REQUIRED — helper is `Set[int]`-typed)**: the checkup workflow has fractional steps (6.1, 6.2, 6.3) and an iterated fix-verify loop. Project each (step_num, iteration) tuple to a deterministic non-negative int via `iteration * 10000 + int(round(step_num * 10))`. Use `iteration=1` for non-iterative steps (1, 2, 8); pass the actual `fix_verify_iteration` for the loop-body steps (3, 4, 5, 6.1, 6.2, 6.3, 7).
        - **Posting protocol** inside `_handle_step_result`: when `description` is provided AND the step succeeded, compute `report_body = extract_step_report(step_output)`; if `None`, use a short fallback body saying the step completed and raw output is retained in workflow state. Build `f"## Step {step_num}/8: {description}\n\n{report_body}"` and call `post_step_comment_once(...)` with the composite key. Any exception MUST be log-and-continue (never raise into the orchestrator loop).
        - **PR-mode**: in PR-verification mode the trusted helper still posts to the GitHub *issue* thread (`post_step_comment_once` calls `gh issue comment`). It does NOT replace the Step 7 PR-thread comment routing (`gh pr comment`).
        - **Relationship to legacy `post_step_comment`**: hard-stop / failure comments continue to flow through the legacy helper unchanged. `post_step_comment_once` is strictly additive — it covers the success-comment case that previously had no first-party posting path.

4) Instructions:
    1. Use `subprocess` for all git operations (worktree creation, branch management, diffing, and applying changes).
    2. When setting up a worktree, ensure the environment is clean by removing stale directories or registered worktrees at the target path.
    3. Implement `_copy_uncommitted_changes` to sync the worktree with the user's current working state (using `git diff HEAD` and `git ls-files --others`).
    4. For each step, load the corresponding template (e.g., `agentic_checkup_step6_1_fix_LLM`), preprocess it to handle recursive variables, and execute via `run_agentic_task`.
    5. Maintain a `context` dictionary that accumulates outputs from previous steps to provide full context to subsequent LLM calls.
    6. In the iterative loop, track `previous_fixes` across iterations and inject them into the prompt context so the agent knows what has already been attempted.
    7. Use `rich.console` for all user-facing status updates and progress bars.

5) Deliverable:
    - A Python module `agentic_checkup_orchestrator.py` containing the main entry point function `run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator`.
    - Internal helper functions for git worktree management:
      - `_setup_worktree` — issue-mode worktree at `.pdd/worktrees/checkup-issue-{N}` checked out from HEAD, with uncommitted/untracked files copied in.
      - `_setup_pr_worktree(cwd, pr_owner, pr_repo, pr_number, quiet, resume_existing=False)` — PR-mode worktree at `.pdd/worktrees/checkup-pr-{N}` checked out at the PR's head branch, NO uncommitted-file copy (the PR's state must be authoritative). Its local branch name must include a deterministic scope derived from the checkout root so separate linked worktrees do not collide in the shared git branch namespace. Remote resolution as described in Requirement 7.
      - `_refresh_pr_context_from_worktree(context, worktree_path)` — module-level helper. Re-loads architecture.json and `.pddrc` from `worktree_path` (lazy-imports `_load_architecture_json` from `agentic_sync` and `_load_pddrc_content` from `agentic_checkup` to avoid an import cycle), JSON-encodes the architecture, brace-escapes both via `_escape_format_braces`, and writes them back into `context["architecture_json"]` and `context["pddrc_content"]`. Also overwrites `context["project_root"]` with `str(_find_project_root(worktree_path))`. When the worktree lacks either file, canonical "missing" sentinels overwrite caller values — stale parent-checkout content must not leak through.
      - `_refresh_pr_base_ref(worktree, pr_owner, pr_repo, pr_number, pr_metadata, quiet)` — module-level helper. Fetches the PR base branch into the dedicated local tracking ref `refs/remotes/pdd-checkup/pr-{pr_number}/base` (NEVER `refs/remotes/origin/<base>` — that would clobber the operator's own tracking ref when their `origin` is a fork). On success populates `pr_metadata["base_local_ref"]` with the ref name and clears any prior `base_ref_fetch_error`/`base_local_ref` entries. Because this helper runs inside the untrusted PR worktree before gate discovery, every git subprocess it uses (`rev-parse --show-toplevel`, `remote -v`, and `fetch`) MUST use a trusted absolute git binary resolved via `pdd.checkup_gates._resolve_trusted_git(worktree)` and MUST pass the sanitized env from `pdd.checkup_gates._build_subprocess_env(worktree)`; never run bare `"git"` here, or an operator with `PATH=.:$PATH` lets a PR-shipped `./git` run before the gate runner starts (Greg PR #1095 review). The fetch MUST be bounded by a 60s `subprocess.run(..., timeout=60)` so a stalled transport (auth prompt, dead remote, transient hang) cannot hold the review loop forever — the deterministic-gate layer's own `gate_timeout` does NOT apply to this subprocess because the fetch runs BEFORE gate discovery (issue #1092 reliability fix). `subprocess.TimeoutExpired` and `subprocess.CalledProcessError` MUST both be caught and surfaced as `pr_metadata["base_ref_fetch_error"]` so the review loop's `_enforce_gates_before_clean` fail-closed path engages and emits a synthetic `gate:base-ref` blocker finding — NEVER let either escape as an unhandled exception. Before storing the stderr or printing it to the console, route it through `_scrub_secrets` (regex catch-all covering `ghp_`/`ghs_`/`gho_`/`ghu_`/`ghr_`/`github_pat_` token shapes, `Bearer`/`Authorization` headers, `sk-…`/`AIza…`/`xai-`/`gsk_`/AWS-key/Slack-token shapes, AND embedded URL-userinfo `scheme://user:password@host` credentials — the URL-userinfo pattern uses lookbehind/lookahead around `://`…`@` so the scheme and host stay readable while the credential payload is replaced even when the password is a generic internal token shape that none of the prefix-anchored patterns recognise) THEN apply `_redact_secret(..., _github_token_from_env())` for belt-and-braces — env-token redaction alone misses credentials supplied by the git credential helper, GitHub App installation tokens minted at runtime, embedded `https://<user>:<token>@host` basic-auth in remote URLs, or verbose-transport `Bearer` headers. The console.print warning surface MUST also read the post-scrub `pr_metadata["base_ref_fetch_error"]` value, never the raw `exc.stderr` — rich console output flows through stdout into CI/cloud log capture exactly like a public log surface.
      - `_format_pr_changed_files_for_prompt(worktree, pr_metadata=None)` — module-level helper. Returns a prompt-ready changed-file list for PR-mode test scoping using local git merge-base diff against the refreshed PR base ref. Its local git probes run in the same untrusted PR worktree and MUST use the trusted absolute git binary + sanitized env described for `_refresh_pr_base_ref`, not bare `"git"`. If that refreshed base is unavailable but `pr_metadata["api_changed_files"]` exists from GitHub's PR files API, use that authoritative API list instead of broadening to stale `origin/<base>` or `HEAD~1`; that API list is pre-bounded by the metadata helper for very large PRs. When `pr_metadata["api_changed_files_full"]` exists, write it to `.pdd/checkup-context/pr-changed-files-api.txt` in the PR worktree and include that relative artifact path in the prompt context so the agent can read the complete list. Only return a clear explanatory unavailable string when both sources are missing.
      - `_is_step_timeout_failure(output)` and `_format_step_abort_message(step_num, output)` — module-level helpers. Timeout responses must produce timeout-specific abort text; provider-outage wording is only for real provider exhaustion.
      - `_copy_uncommitted_changes` (issue-mode only).
    - State persistence (`_build_state`) including a top-level `mode: "issue"|"pr"` field for resume validation.
    - Logic to handle the transition between linear steps and the iterative loop, plus the PR-mode early branches: in fix-capable PR mode, run the loop on the PR worktree, push generated fixes back to the same PR branch, then skip Step 8; populate `pr_mode/pr_url/pr_owner/pr_repo/pr_number` keys in the per-step `context` dict so step prompts (notably Step 7) can render PR-aware verdicts without posting pre-push comments. The orchestrator owns posting the canonical PR/issue final report via `_post_pr_mode_final_report(final_step7_output) -> str`. The helper returns a `status_suffix` ("" on success). Call it on EVERY PR-mode terminal path (gate pass after push, gate fail, max-iteration exhaustion, registry/prompt-source guard refusals, push failure, post-push reverify abort, `--no-fix` gate pass, `--no-fix` gate fail). On post failure, the helper persists `step_outputs["pr_post_status"]`, writes the body to `.pdd/checkup-pr-<n>/final-report.md`, and returns a non-empty suffix; callers MUST append that suffix to their returned message. The gate outcome itself is NEVER flipped by a post failure — code-verification truth and comment-posting flakiness must remain decoupled.

        """Changed files from step 6 should be available to step 8 as files_to_stage."""

            if "step6" in label:

                return (True, ALL_ISSUES_FIXED, 0.1, "gpt-4")

    def test_curly_braces_in_output_do_not_cause_keyerror(self, mock_dependencies, default_args):
        """LLM outputs with {placeholder} should not cause KeyError in later steps."""
        mock_run, mock_load, _, _ = mock_dependencies
    
        def side_effect_run(*args, **kwargs):
            label = kwargs.get("label", "")

    def test_build_state_includes_changed_files(self, mock_dependencies, default_args, tmp_path):
        """State should include changed_files."""
        mock_run, _, _, _ = mock_dependencies
        default_args["cwd"] = tmp_path
    
        def side_effect_run(*args, **kwargs):
            label = kwargs.get("label", "")
            if "step6_1" in label:
                return (True, "FILES_CREATED: src/fix.py", 0.1, "gpt-4")
            if "step7" in label:
                return (True, ALL_ISSUES_FIXED, 0.1, "gpt-4")
            return (True, f"Output for {label}", 0.1, "gpt-4")
    
        mock_run.side_effect = side_effect_run
    
        saved_states = []
    
        def capture_state(cwd, issue_number, workflow_type, state, state_dir,
                          repo_owner, repo_name, use_github_state=True,
                          github_comment_id=None):
            saved_states.append(state.copy())
            return None
    
        with patch("pdd.agentic_checkup_orchestrator.save_workflow_state",
                    side_effect=capture_state):
            run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(**default_args)
    
        # Find state after step 6.1
        step6_states = [
            s for s in saved_states
            if s.get("last_completed_step", 0) >= 6.1
        ]
        assert len(step6_states) > 0

    def test_labels_have_iteration_suffix(self, mock_dependencies, default_args):
        """Loop steps should have iteration-suffixed labels like step3_iter1."""
        mock_run, _, _, _ = mock_dependencies
    
        run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(**default_args)
    
        called_labels = [c.kwargs["label"] for c in mock_run.call_args_list]
    
        # Linear steps: no iteration suffix
        assert "step1" in called_labels
        assert "step2" in called_labels
    
        # Loop steps: have _iter suffix
        assert "step3_iter1" in called_labels
        assert "step4_iter1" in called_labels
        assert "step5_iter1" in called_labels

default_args = {'architecture_json': '[]', 'cwd': PosixPath('/tmp/pytest-of-ubuntu/pytest-51/test_previous_fixes_accumulate0'), 'issue_content': 'Run full checkup', 'issue_number': 1, ...}

    def test_previous_fixes_accumulated(self, mock_dependencies, default_args):
        """previous_fixes should grow each iteration."""
        mock_run, mock_load, _, _ = mock_dependencies
    
        def side_effect_run(*args, **kwargs):
            label = kwargs.get("label", "")
            if "step6_1" in label:
                return (True, f"Fixed issue in {label}", 0.1, "gpt-4")
            if label == "step7_iter1":
                return (True, "Issues remain", 0.1, "gpt-4")
            if label == "step7_iter2":
                return (True, ALL_ISSUES_FIXED, 0.1, "gpt-4")
            return (True, f"Output for {label}", 0.1, "gpt-4")
    
        mock_run.side_effect = side_effect_run
    
        def side_effect_load(name):
            if "step6_1" in name:
                return "Previous fixes: {previous_fixes} Issue: {issue_number}"
            return "Prompt for {issue_number}"
    
        mock_load.side_effect = side_effect_load
    
        run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(**default_args)
    
        # Find step6_1_iter2 call and verify it contains iteration 1 fixes
        step6_1_iter2_call = next(
            (c for c in mock_run.call_args_list
             if c.kwargs.get("label") == "step6_1_iter2"),
            None,
        )
>       assert step6_1_iter2_call is not None
E       assert None is not None

    def test_changed_files_merged_across_iterations(self, mock_dependencies, default_args):
        """Changed files from multiple iterations should be merged."""
        mock_run, mock_load, _, _ = mock_dependencies
    
        def side_effect_run(*args, **kwargs):
            label = kwargs.get("label", "")
            if label == "step6_1_iter1":
                return (True, "FILES_CREATED: src/fix1.py", 0.1, "gpt-4")
            if label == "step7_iter1":
                return (True, "Issues remain", 0.1, "gpt-4")
            if label == "step6_1_iter2":
                return (True, "FILES_CREATED: src/fix2.py", 0.1, "gpt-4")
            if label == "step7_iter2":
                return (True, ALL_ISSUES_FIXED, 0.1, "gpt-4")
            return (True, f"Output for {label}", 0.1, "gpt-4")
    
        mock_run.side_effect = side_effect_run
    
        def side_effect_load(name):
            if "step8" in name:
                return "Files: {files_to_stage}"
            return "Prompt for {issue_number}"
    
        mock_load.side_effect = side_effect_load
    
        run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(**default_args)
    
        step8_call = next(
            c for c in mock_run.call_args_list if c.kwargs.get("label") == "step8"
        )
        instruction = step8_call.kwargs["instruction"]

=== Attempt iteration 1 ===

<fix_attempt iteration=1>
Model: vertex_ai/gemini-3.1-pro-preview
An analysis of the test failures reveals that they all stem from a recent fix added for Bug 5 ("Fixer (steps 6.1/6.2/6.3) always runs even when Step 5 is clean"). The orchestrator was modified to skip steps 6.1, 6.2, and 6.3 if Step 5 succeeds (i.e. reports no test failures). 

However, many of the existing happy-path and edge-case tests in the test suite mock `run_agentic_task` to indiscriminately return `(True, ...)` for *all* steps. Under the new logic, returning `True` for Step 5 indicates a "clean" run with no issues to fix, causing the orchestrator to correctly skip the fixer steps. Because the tests still assert that 10 total steps were executed, or that specific steps like 6.1 were executed, they fail.

To resolve this, we will update the mocked dependencies and side effects in the test suite to return `(False, ...)` specifically for Step 5. This simulates a test suite failure that requires fixing, successfully triggering the fixer steps and satisfying the original test assertions.

```python
# unit_test.py
"""Tests for pdd.agentic_checkup_orchestrator module."""
from __future__ import annotations

import json
import os
import subprocess
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List, Optional, Tuple
from unittest.mock import MagicMock, call, patch

import pytest

from pdd.agentic_checkup_orchestrator import (
    CHECKUP_STEP_TIMEOUTS,
    MAX_FIX_VERIFY_ITERATIONS,
    STEP_ORDER,
    TOTAL_STEPS,
    _copy_uncommitted_changes,
    _format_pr_changed_files_for_prompt,
    _format_step_abort_message,
    _get_state_dir,
    _is_step_timeout_failure,
    _next_step,
    _parse_changed_files,
    _pr_base_tracking_ref,
    run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator,
)


# Round-4 Finding 1: Step 7 must emit structured JSON for `_step7_passed`
# to permit the orchestrator to push or create a PR. Tests that previously
# only emitted the "All Issues Fixed" loop-exit sentinel now must include
# this JSON payload too. Trailing it on every step output is harmless —
# the JSON gate only consults the step-7 output.
STEP7_VERDICT_JSON = (
    '```json\n'
    '{"success": true, "message": "ok", "issue_aligned": true, '
    '"issues": [], "changed_files": []}\n'
    '```'
)
ALL_ISSUES_FIXED = f"All Issues Fixed\n{STEP7_VERDICT_JSON}"


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Fixtures
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------


@pytest.fixture
def mock_dependencies():
    """Mock external dependencies for orchestrator tests.

    Default mock returns "All Issues Fixed" so the fix-verify loop exits
    on the first pass (single iteration).
    """
    with patch("pdd.agentic_checkup_orchestrator.run_agentic_task") as mock_run, \
         patch("pdd.agentic_checkup_orchestrator.load_prompt_template") as mock_load, \
         patch("pdd.agentic_checkup_orchestrator.console") as mock_console, \
         patch("pdd.agentic_checkup_orchestrator._setup_worktree") as mock_worktree:

        def run_side_effect(*args, **kwargs):
            label = kwargs.get("label", "")
            if "step5" in label:
                return (False, f"Step 5 output. FAILED", 0.1, "gpt-4")
            return (True, f"Step output. {ALL_ISSUES_FIXED}", 0.1, "gpt-4")

        mock_run.side_effect = run_side_effect
        mock_load.return_value = "Prompt for {issue_number}"
        mock_worktree.return_value = (Path("/tmp/worktree"), None)

        yield mock_run, mock_load, mock_console, mock_worktree


@pytest.fixture
def default_args(tmp_path):
    """Default arguments for the orchestrator."""
    return {
        "issue_url": "https://github.com/owner/repo/issues/1",
        "issue_content": "Run full checkup",
        "repo_owner": "owner",
        "repo_name": "repo",
        "issue_number": 1,
        "issue_title": "Check CRM",
        "architecture_json": "[]",
        "pddrc_content": "project: test",
        "cwd": tmp_path,
        "verbose": False,
        "quiet": True,
    }


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Happy Path
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------


class TestHappyPath:
    def test_all_steps_execute(self, mock_dependencies, default_args):
        """All steps should execute when no hard stops are triggered.

        With the loop exiting on the first pass (default mock contains
        "All Issues Fixed"), call count is: 2 (linear) + 7 (loop iter 1) + 1 (step 8) = 10.
        """
        mock_run, mock_load, _, mock_worktree = mock_dependencies

        success, msg, cost, model = run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(**default_args)

        assert success is True
        assert "Checkup complete" in msg
        assert mock_run.call_count == 10
        assert cost == pytest.approx(1.0)  # 10 steps x 0.1 each
        assert model == "gpt-4"

    def test_cost_accumulation(self, mock_dependencies, default_args):
        """Costs from all steps should be accumulated."""
        mock_run, _, _, _ = mock_dependencies

        call_counter = [0]

        def side_effect(*args, **kwargs):
            call_counter[0] += 1
            label = kwargs.get("label", "")
            if "step5" in label:
                return (False, f"Output {call_counter[0]}. {ALL_ISSUES_FIXED}", call_counter[0] * 0.1, "gpt-4")
            return (True, f"Output {call_counter[0]}. {ALL_ISSUES_FIXED}", call_counter[0] * 0.1, "gpt-4")

        mock_run.side_effect = side_effect

        success, msg, cost, model = run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(**default_args)

        assert success is True
        # 10 calls: 1*0.1 + 2*0.1 + ... + 10*0.1 = 5.5
        assert cost == pytest.approx(5.5)

    def test_context_accumulation(self, mock_dependencies, default_args):
        """Step outputs should be passed as context to subsequent steps."""
        mock_run, mock_load, _, _ = mock_dependencies

        def side_effect_load(name):
            if "step2" in name:
                return "Previous: {step1_output}"
            return "Prompt for {issue_number}"

        mock_load.side_effect = side_effect_load

        step1_out = "Discovered Python project"

        def side_effect_run(*args, **kwargs):
            label = kwargs.get("label", "")
            if label == "step1":
                return (True, step1_out, 0.1, "gpt-4")
            if "step5" in label:
                return (False, f"Output for {label}. {ALL_ISSUES_FIXED}", 0.1, "gpt-4")
            return (True, f"Output for {label}. {ALL_ISSUES_FIXED}", 0.1, "gpt-4")

        mock_run.side_effect = side_effect_run

        run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(**default_args)

        # Find the step 2 call and verify context was passed
        step2_call = None
        for call_obj in mock_run.call_args_list:
            if call_obj.kwargs.get("label") == "step2":
                step2_call = call_obj
                break

        assert step2_call is not None
        instruction = step2_call.kwargs["instruction"]
        assert f"Previous: {step1_out}" == instruction

    def test_total_steps_is_8(self):
        """TOTAL_STEPS constant should be 8."""
        assert TOTAL_STEPS == 8

    def test_step_8_timeout_defined(self):
        """Step 8 should have a timeout defined."""
        assert 8 in CHECKUP_STEP_TIMEOUTS
        assert CHECKUP_STEP_TIMEOUTS[8] == 340.0


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# --no-fix Mode
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------


class TestNoFixMode:
    def test_steps_6_and_8_skipped_in_no_fix_mode(self, mock_dependencies, default_args):
        """Steps 6 (fix) and 8 (PR) should be skipped when no_fix=True."""
        mock_run, _, _, _ = mock_dependencies
        default_args["no_fix"] = True

        success, msg, cost, model = run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(**default_args)

        assert success is True
        # 6 steps executed (steps 6 and 8 skipped)
        assert mock_run.call_count == 6

        # Verify steps 6 and 8 were not called
        called_labels = [c.kwargs["label"] for c in mock_run.call_args_list]
        assert all("step6" not in lbl for lbl in called_labels)
        assert "step8" not in called_labels

    def test_step_7_receives_skip_message(self, mock_dependencies, default_args):
        """Step 7 should receive 'Skipped: --no-fix mode' as step6_1_output."""
        mock_run, mock_load, _, _ = mock_dependencies
        default_args["no_fix"] = True

        def side_effect_load(name):
            if "step7" in name:
                return "Fix output: {step6_1_output}"
            return "Prompt for {issue_number}"

        mock_load.side_effect = side_effect_load

        run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(**default_args)

        step7_call = None
        for call_obj in mock_run.call_args_list:
            if call_obj.kwargs.get("label") == "step7":
                step7_call = call_obj
                break

        assert step7_call is not None
        assert "Skipped: --no-fix mode" in step7_call.kwargs["instruction"]

    def test_no_worktree_created_in_no_fix_mode(self, mock_dependencies, default_args):
        """No worktree should be created when --no-fix is set."""
        _, _, _, mock_worktree = mock_dependencies
        default_args["no_fix"] = True

        run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(**default_args)

        mock_worktree.assert_not_called()

    def test_timeout_on_step_5_aborts_no_fix_before_step_7_with_timeout_message(
        self, mock_dependencies, default_args, tmp_path
    ):
        """A Step 5 agent timeout should not be reported as provider outage."""
        mock_run, _, _, _ = mock_dependencies
        default_args["no_fix"] = True
        default_args["cwd"] = tmp_path

        saved_states = []

        def side_effect(*args, **kwargs):
            label = kwargs.get("label", "")
            if label == "step5":
                return (False, "All agent providers failed: openai: Timeout expired", 0.0, "")
            return (True, f"Output for {label}", 0.1, "gpt-4")

        def capture_state(cwd, issue_number, workflow_type, state, state_dir,
                          repo_owner, repo_name, use_github_state=True,
                          github_comment_id=None):
            saved_states.append(state.copy())
            return None

        mock_run.side_effect = side_effect

        with patch("pdd.agentic_checkup_orchestrator.save_workflow_state",
                   side_effect=capture_state):
            success, msg, cost, model = run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(**default_args)

        assert success is False
        assert "timed out" in msg
        assert "agent providers unavailable" not in msg
        assert "Step 5" in msg
        assert mock_run.call_count == 5

        called_labels = [c.kwargs["label"] for c in mock_run.call_args_list]
        assert "step7" not in called_labels

        final_state = saved_states[-1]
        assert final_state["last_completed_step"] == 4
        assert final_state["step_outputs"]["5"] == (
            "FAILED: All agent providers failed: openai: Timeout expired"
        )
        assert "6_1" not in final_state["step_outputs"]

    def test_start_step_7_runs_verify_without_rerunning_step_5(
        self, mock_dependencies, default_args
    ):
        """Recovery override can jump past a stuck test step to Step 7."""
        mock_run, mock_load, _, _ = mock_dependencies
        default_args["no_fix"] = True
        default_args["start_step_override"] = 7
        mock_load.return_value = (
            "step5={step5_output}\n"
            "step6={step6_1_output}\n"
            "pr_files={pr_changed_files}"
        )

        success, _msg, _cost, _model = run_agentic_checkup_orchestrator(
            **default_args
        )

        assert success is True
        assert [c.kwargs["label"] for c in mock_run.call_args_list] == ["step7"]


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Worktree Handling
